  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ba82cbb5-65ac-4431-99ee-f9ad150c528b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText888807989138393679" style="display:none">Beware!<br /><br />Dangerous secrets lie between the pages of this book.<br /><br />OK, I warned you. But if you think I'll give anything away, or tell you that this is the sequel to my first literary endeavor, <i>The Name of This Book is Secret</i>, you're wrong.<br /><br />I'm not going to remind you of how we last left our heroes, Cass and Max-Ernest, as they awaited intiation into the mysterious Terces Society, or the ongoing fight against the evil Dr. L and Ms. Mauvais. I certainly won't be telling you about how the kids stumble upon the Museum of Magic, where they finally meet the amazing Pietro!<br /><br />Oh, blast! I've done it again. Well, at least I didn't tell you about the missing Sound Prism, the nefarious Lord Pharaoh, or the mysterious creature born in a bottle over 500 years ago, the key to the biggest secret of all.<br /><br />I really can't help myself, now can I? Let's face it - if you're reading this, it's too late.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36857462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer953648454306579738">Reviewed by LaLeesha Haynes for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>This is a fun book with an interesting narrative. Cass and Max-Ernest are young adults who have recently been involved with a secret society, the details of which are located in the previous book in the series. Although you do miss out on some details of the protagonists, you could read this book without having read the previous installment, THE NAME OF THIS BOOK IS SECRET. <br/><br/>When you read IF YOU'RE READING THIS, IT'S TOO LATE, it is as though you ar</span>
  <span id="freeText953648454306579738" style="display:none">Reviewed by LaLeesha Haynes for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />This is a fun book with an interesting narrative. Cass and Max-Ernest are young adults who have recently been involved with a secret society, the details of which are located in the previous book in the series. Although you do miss out on some details of the protagonists, you could read this book without having read the previous installment, THE NAME OF THIS BOOK IS SECRET. <br /><br />When you read IF YOU'RE READING THIS, IT'S TOO LATE, it is as though you are being told a story by the campfire. <br /><br />The characters are well-developed, easy to relate to, and have a good sense of humor. Because of the short chapters and common footnotes, I see this as a great book for a reluctant reader. It is easy to pick up where you left off and it takes you down many paths at once, keeping you interested. The footnotes typically add a humorous aspect to an interesting mystery, allowing the reader to venture in a new direction before continuing on with the story. <br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this book. It had a strong storyline with characters that took risks and maintained and created friendships. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="953648454306579738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer978731820317959697">(You should probably read the first book of the series, "The Name of This Book is Secret," if you haven't done so. It will give you a better understanding of what this book is going to be about.) Anyways...<br/><br/> "If You're Reading This, it's Too Late," by Pseudonymous Bosch is another mysterious and adventurous book following the previous book. Once again, Cass and Max-Ernest are set on a mission to find the Secret, but more importantly (this time,) the homunculus. In the beginning of Cass and Max- E</span>
  <span id="freeText978731820317959697" style="display:none">(You should probably read the first book of the series, "The Name of This Book is Secret," if you haven't done so. It will give you a better understanding of what this book is going to be about.) Anyways...<br /><br /> "If You're Reading This, it's Too Late," by Pseudonymous Bosch is another mysterious and adventurous book following the previous book. Once again, Cass and Max-Ernest are set on a mission to find the Secret, but more importantly (this time,) the homunculus. In the beginning of Cass and Max- Ernest's journey, a new boy named Yoji (nicknamed Yo-Yoji (for saying "yo" so much)) come into class. On a field trip, while Cass and Max-Ernest are still on their quest, Yo-Yoji bugs the two collaborators so much just to know what the "Secret" Cass and Max- Ernest were talking about. However, Cass manages to shoo away Yo-Yoji, so that the two can finish their mission. This time, their mission is very important because they are part of the Terces Society (Secret spelled backwards.)<br /> Apparently, the Midnight Sun (as known as the enemy), tricks Cass and Max- Ernest into coming into their ship. After being tied up and held as prisoners, Cass and Max- Ernest manage to break free. However, you have to read the book to find out why the homunculus was so important and that the Secret was. <br /> I would suggest this book to those who like to read in suspense and mystery. Don't give up now! You will )someday figure out the Secret.<br /> The next book of these series, (the Secret Series,) is "This Book is Not Good for You," (I think I can tell you're questioning why there are so many weird titles. <br /> if you want to read an adventure full of mystery and suspense, read this book!<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristi-Lael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristi-Lael" href="/user/show/5421449-cristi-lael">Cristi-Lael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2612800175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2612800175" />
    <a title="Carson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89686706-carson"><img alt="Carson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542979167p2/89686706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2612800175?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carson" href="/user/show/89686706-carson">Carson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316113687" href="/book/show/6738624-if-you-re-reading-this-it-s-too-late">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89686706-carson?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89686706-carson?shelf=lemony">lemony</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89686706-carson?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89686706-carson?shelf=sequel">sequel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2612800175&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2612800175" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9275530695186892141"><i>“Only bad books have good endings.<br/>If a book is any good, it's ending is always bad - because you don't want the book to end.”</i><br/><br/>Remember how much I gushed about the first book? I forgot to say that I couldn't wait for the second. More lore within the series' secretive universe, more character development, and more adventure and some new magical artifact. It would be an understatement to say that my expectations for the second book in the Secret Series were higher than a kite. Did it live up to thos</span>
  <span id="freeText9275530695186892141" style="display:none"><i>“Only bad books have good endings.<br />If a book is any good, it's ending is always bad - because you don't want the book to end.”</i><br /><br />Remember how much I gushed about the first book? I forgot to say that I couldn't wait for the second. More lore within the series' secretive universe, more character development, and more adventure and some new magical artifact. It would be an understatement to say that my expectations for the second book in the Secret Series were higher than a kite. Did it live up to those expectations? (yeah, as if the two star rating didn't clue you in already, right?) Find out in my review of If You're Reading This, It's Too Late.<br /><br />So after we get a scene of the Midnight Sun breaking into what I can assume is a magic gallery of sorts (in black pages and white text, a nice touch), the author slacks off and then we are introduced to Cassandra, who is having a strange dream. She talks to her friend Max-Ernest about her dream, only for us to get more flat humor (a dream is the fulfillment of a wish/fish! I know, referencing Sigmund Freud is kind of intelligent, but there's something about this sentence Bosch throws in that seems...dumb, I guess?).<br /><br />So Amber being Amber, decides to mess with our heroes by claiming they're a couple. Obviously, this does not go over well with Cass, whose ears (she has this weird thing where her ears change color depending on her mood) grow red, which means she's mad. Yo-Yoji is at their school as well and wants to make friends with them, but Max-Ernest is too pissed to care.<br /><br />So then, the class goes to the tide pools, and this is where things get interesting. Cass and Max-Ernest slip away from the class and head off to a wharf, where they then reach Dock 3 (a location they were told to visit via code). They find an extremely lavish, fancy black boat that stops in front of them. Now, I want you to answer this for me. Which of the three do our protagonists do?<br /><br />A: Do they realize who the boat really belongs to and make a break for it?<br />B: Do they get on the boat?<br />Or C: Do they go out for hot dogs and get a haircut, before finally checking into an expensive hotel?<br /><br />If you were guessing C, then you're wrong. They get on the boat.<br />Which makes me realize that these two are dumber than a sack of acorns. With a boat as garish as that one, how would you not think that it would belong to the Midnight Sun? Heck—how didn't they see the flag?! I'm pretty sure they were raised so you could clearly see them! But, plot, I guess...<br /><br />So as it turns out, the guy claiming to be Pietro is really Dr. L, and we meet the Skelton Sisters, who have the opportunity of saving Cass and Max-Ernest, but are distracted by her sock monster (remember this scene). Ms. Mauvais demands to know about a "Homunculus" and tells the kids to "stop playing dumb", even though they really know nothing about it. They get thrown into one of the ship's rooms, and Max-Ernest, who, unlike Cass, actually has a plan to escape, tries to free them both but Cass (unsuprisingly) is being difficult. She strongly disbelieves of Max-Ernest's Houdini act (which is his escape plan) and keeps counterwriggling his wriggles and keeps saying generally nasty things, which all display Cass's huge character flaw of pride and a big mouth.<br /><br />But Max-Ernest actually does get them out, and Cass half-admits she was wrong ("I guess those magic books weren't such a waste of time, after all, she says). Then they read about the Homunculus and find the Sound Prism, and then they stumble back onto the deck in the middle of the night and are saved by their wildlife preserves teacher, Mr. Needleman, who is actually Owen in disguise. So Owen gets them away from the ocean and drives them back home, where he shows absolutely no sympathy for Cass worrying he'll be replaced at school with some boring teacher who is mean naturally and not just acting like it, which, thankfully, is a small blow to Cass's already-oversized ego.<br /><br />So Max-Ernest wants to go back home for some reason (won't his parents punish him for abandoning class...?) but Cass wants to find the Magic Museum while they still can. After they solve another riddle, they travel into another room and meet the main members of the society. Pietro, the old magician of whose notebook Cass and Max-Ernest had read (I wonder what happened to that notebook, by the way), Lily Wei, a Chinese girl referenced in the first book who is now all grown up, and Mr. Wallace, a sad-looking man who I've always imagined had sort of a Droopy voice.<br /><br />So Pietro tells them that they must protect the Sound Prism, and everyone objects on the grounds that it's dangerous. Which brings me to my first question: What does the Terces Society <i>do</i>, exactly? Okay, I mean, I know they protect the Secret from the Midnight Sun, but you'd think they'd do what they can to help out the kids. Owen literally says at one point, "It does seem dangerous...not that I'm volunteering...", which makes me wonder—if these guys are trying to protect this Secret, then why don't they help out with this instead of archiving all the time? In fact, I now must ask, why are Cass and Max-Ernest doing this? What do they have to do with any of this? These two were picked out of a regular bunch of children and are only on this mission because they were interested in Pietro's story in Book One. They have no reason to care, especially because...<br /><br />Ms. Mauvais said in Book One that the Secret was the secret to immortality. So now I have two more questions:<br /><br />1. Don't they have elixirs that make them live forever anyway? So then why do they need the Secret?<br />2. What's so bad about these guys being immortal?! They already are! They have their elixirs. That makes them keep living. If they get their hands on the Secret, so what? How will it destroy the world if these guys live forever? At this point, it seems like Cass and Max-Ernest's ordeal is more of a chore than a mission.<br /><br />So after they leave the Magic Museum, Cass returns back home, where she is grounded. And she should be...because both she and Max-Ernest are MORONS!<br /><br />By going home, Cass is grounded for the rest of the year. Why did she go back? Wouldn't it have made more sense to stay away from home until you got the whole Sound Prism business over with? You'd have more freedom if you'd just avoided going back home altogether. But, plot, I guess. Either that or Cass is an idiot. I choose both.<br /><br />We never get to see what happens to Max-Ernest, so I assume he wasn't punished.<br /><br />So, anyway, Owen writes an offensive letter to Cass and Max-Ernest's school that basically screws the two dimwits over even further, which makes me now realize how much of a douche he is (why did he write this letter? For what reason? Was it so they'd be forced to stay in school? I don't know why).<br /><br />So Cass has Yoji (Oh, I'm sorry, YO-Yoji) solve a puzzle concerning the Sound Prism despite Max-Ernest saying that they can't tell anyone else about what they're doing, but Cass shoots out a few soothing choice words ("We didn't take the oath [of the Terces Society], did we?" and "Let him try at least!") to shut him up. Max, as a friend, I have to say, please don't try to stop her from breaking the rules. She'll only start whining more.<br /><br />So to my surprise, Yoji (I'm just going to refer to him as Yoji here on out, because Yo-Yoji sounds utterly freaking stupid) solves the puzzle-it's CABBAGE FACE), and Max-Ernest starts to feel a little left out and depressed. Cass was his first friend, and he felt that she was being taken away from him (I'd consider it a gift from the heavens).<br /><br />So when Max-Ernest gets home after dumping Cass (i.e., he stops being friends with her), we get some seriously depressing lines such as "it was strange to have made a friend in the first place" and "Max-Ernest wished he'd never made a friend", and I just feel so bad for this guy, especially because his arc is done away with AND IT NEVER GETS FINISHED! Just when it feels like we're digging deep into his emotions, he finds some hidden file about the Homunculus's backstory, he shows it to Cass, and his arc is thrown out the window.<br /><br />And of course, rather than be warm and understanding whilst forgiving Max-Ernest, Cass finds that some cold, bossy complaining would suffice. She basically says that Max-Ernest is still her collaborator and still part of the Terces Society, he's just "being crazy" and "acting jealous" because of Yoji. Thanks for that, Cass.<br /><br />Oh, and as a side note, the book tries to justify Max-Ernest's mistreatment by saying that "you could say things like that without hurting [Max-Ernest's] feelings". But why would you want to?<br /><br />Cass has another dream and reads about a boy named Tommy meeting a bear at Whisper Lake (which, I must admit, is a nice callback to the beginning of the book where there's an article on Cass's wall headlined "BEAR OR BIGFOOT?") and has her grandfather's take her, Max-Ernest and Yoji on a camping trip to that very location. Cass calls the Homunculus with the Sound Prism that night, and the Homunculus arrives, demanding to know if Cass is the person who deserves to call him. He tells her to give him the Jester's real name so he can prove it. But here's my question: If Cass is the only person who can use this Sound Prism, then why does he need to know if she's the rightful heir to the Jester? I believe that Pietro said that only Cass can use the Sound Prism and answered, "you will see" and the reason turned out to be because Cass is the rightful heir. So why does the Homunculus need to do this inspection if only the rightful heir can use it?<br /><br />Furthermore, The Legend of Cabbage Face explains that the Homunculus has responded to the beck and call of anyone who's summoned him, so it's not only Cass who can use it. This makes even less sense when you realize that Max-Ernest and Yoji used it to hear what Cass was saying when she got captured by the Midnight Sun, and to create a sonic boom, and Pietro used it to fool the Midnight Sun Members into not opening Lord Pharaoh's grave. But I digress. By a wide margin. Besides, if I tried to list all the plotholes in this book, I'd be here all day.<br /><br />So then there's this sort of irritating scene where Yoji asks why Max-Ernest "hates on him all the time" and doesn't allow him to explain himself because jerk, and then they have to solve a Greek Mythology puzzle which Max-Ernest (of course) succeeds in doing. Cass and her friends get back to the Magic Museum to find that the Homunculus has escaped due to Cass lying about there being food there. In the midst of Cass's distress, Amber records the Sound Prism song, which plays because Cass attempts to call the Homunculus again. So Cass decides they need to go the Skelton Sisters concert because she heard Amber talking to Veronica in the bathroom, and when they get there the Homunculus is called via song and then he and Cass are captured.<br /><br />Now, let's be honest: the Homunculus is nowhere near as powerful as the narrative makes him look. What exactly does he do once you call him? This guy has no special powers of any kind, just a need to eat. There's even a joke made about it when he (very briefly) fools Cass into thinking she gets three wishes, only to deny this theory and ask why people always expect that from him. So then what in the heck does he do, then? What's his power? Why would you need to call him? Just a small question.<br /><br />So then they find Cass at a graveyard and this epic battle breaks out. Now, I'm not exaggerating when I say this is the most well done part of the book, or even the only really well done scene. I loved the circies and carnies being themselves while kicking some Midnight butt, as well as Lily getting her revenge on Ms. Mauvais. This entire scene was just amazing and the least forgettable aspect of the book.<br /><br />When Cass gets home, it's revealed that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she is a foundling <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which would have made for a sweet, atmospheric ending...<br /><br />Were it not for the Talent Show chapter...<br /><br />I pretty much half-skimmed this one, as it's basically full of the shameless anti-Max-Ernest propaganda that the series is undeniably good at. This chapter was nothing but filler and only throws in a dumb joke that basically says that only Max-Ernest's parents could love his jokes, Cass being the most unsupportive little brat and being relieved when she thought her friend was backing out, being relieved again when her savior Yoji comes in and shows off how "cool" he is, and thinks to herself "maybe [Max-Ernest] won't be such a disaster after all".<br /><br />What do I think of this book? It's clearly not as good as the first. Dr. L and Ms. Mauvais have been regressed to simple, pathetic villains who are less determined in their goals, the Homunculus is basically a walking fat joke (loves to eat, eats very sloppily), and Yoji? Hoo, boy do I have a lot to talk about.<br /><br />Why did we end up getting this miserable excuse for a character? Well, it's because the Terces Society asked him to watch over Cass and Max-Ernest for some weird reason. But my question is, how did he get to know about the Terces Society? How did he meet Lily? What does he have to do with any of this? Why did they tell him to watch Cass and Max-Ernest? I literally do not get why he exists. His personality is flat. He's basically the "cool teen" stereotype, which has been done to death. His language consists of nothing but "yo", "dude", "chill", and "bro". Yoji is so flat and stereotypical in his role that I kept reading him with a Roger Craig Smith voice because it would definitely suit such a stereotypically "cool" character. I could see why Max-Ernest hated him so much, because he was annoying!<br /><br />I would've like it better if there was this huge misunderstanding and another girl had been chosen to protect the secret. She always upstaged and humiliated Cass and deflated her ego and was much closer to Max-Ernest, acting as a big sister to him ironically enjoying his terrible jokes. She would attack Cass's pride with half-awareness, and Cass lets this flaw get the best of her. But I guess we got Yoji 'cause we gotta be hip with the times.<br /><br />The plot of this one wasn't as well thought out as the first book. There were more holes in it than Swiss cheese. Not only that, but it's also much more light-hearted than the first book. This book has all these "wacky" jokes utilized for cheap laughs and it loses that dark, foreboding feel that the first book managed to cultivate. The illustrations, while not very good in Book One, are even worse here. There seems to be a semblance of old film effects on the illustrations that suggest a film noir look. Nice touch. And at least the prose is still amazing.<br /><br />So, no. This book does not live up to the first. It does a terrible job. But I will admit that it's okay as a standalone book. Like, if you pick it up off the shelf without reading the series, it's a fine read. But as a sequel, it's tremendously lacking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9275530695186892141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3157111781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3157111781" />
    <a title="Ross Eberle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/96774492-ross-eberle"><img alt="Ross Eberle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557099530p2/96774492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3157111781?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ross Eberle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ross Eberle" href="/user/show/96774492-ross-eberle">Ross Eberle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3157111781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11255045874854930620">Prologue: No, Bosch, you are NOT the greatest writer of all time. So, don't even suggest it. Also, what on God's Green Ethical Earth would entice you to suggest eating an animal!? o_o<br/><br/>Pardon me, Sir, but are you ****ing bonkers!? No matter. I still pretty much like you.<br/>Now onto the review of your book...<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3359940.If_You_re_Reading_This__It_s_Too_Late__Secret___2_' title='If You're Reading This, It's Too Late (Secret, #2) by Pseudonymous Bosch' rel='nofollow noopener'>If You're Reading This, It's Too Late</a> pretty much effectively continues the stories of the child-heroes, Cass and Max-Earnest from where the first book left off. The story itself is quite good and</span>
  <span id="freeText11255045874854930620" style="display:none">Prologue: No, Bosch, you are NOT the greatest writer of all time. So, don't even suggest it. Also, what on God's Green Ethical Earth would entice you to suggest eating an animal!? o_o<br /><br />Pardon me, Sir, but are you ****ing bonkers!? No matter. I still pretty much like you.<br />Now onto the review of your book...<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3359940.If_You_re_Reading_This__It_s_Too_Late__Secret___2_" title="If You're Reading This, It's Too Late (Secret, #2) by Pseudonymous Bosch" rel="nofollow noopener">If You're Reading This, It's Too Late</a> pretty much effectively continues the stories of the child-heroes, Cass and Max-Earnest from where the first book left off. The story itself is quite good and has just a hint of actual fantasy contained within it (I.E. The Homonculus). And if you're one of my Superior-Fans, then you know how much I love a good fantasy read.<br /><br />And since we're now on the subject-matter of this book, I am rather fond of the world-building of this novel, as well as the last one. Even though it's only on Earth, but it's not without its charm! Plus, the way the characters are portrayed is on a level not often seen in a story like this. My favorite heroine will always be Cass. Can you blame me? She's a survivalist!! Plus, the humor this book includes almost had me rolling on the floor, laughing copters!!... Almost...<br /><br />And now onto the...Not-so-good points which are comprised of this book...<br />1: The flatulence...Yuck! Mr. Bosch, you don't need to include this in your works, do you? O_O I mean, it's bad enough you stuck it blatantly in your first novel...I mean, c'mon!!<br />2: Though I know you were trying to be funny, why of all the critters did you have the sock-people portrayed as...Roaches!? I mean, seriously!! Those are just gross. And they carry the Cholera!<br />3: I felt the ending of this book was too sudden and abrupt. It just left the reader (I.E. me) hanging there and wondering to himself: Wait, is this it? Kinda reminds me of the ending of The Birds II: Land's End. Guesh I'm gonna have to read Book 3 to find out what comes next, eh?<br /><br />Epilogue: You won't tell us your real name. In fact, you flat out REFUSE to tell us your real name. Nay, you downright threaten to KILL us if we keep on pressing the question!? What is wrong with you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/543080.Pseudonymous_Bosch" title="Pseudonymous Bosch" rel="nofollow noopener">Pseudonymous Bosch</a>!? If you don't quit sticking dumb, disgusting things in your works (You know what I mean), I'll send my Sky Fighters to kill you, instead!!...<br />...Ha!! Just kidding!...Or am I? o_o Any thoughts on this, Mr. Bosch?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11255045874854930620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer357748829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4861020228151253068">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a> <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Short and Simple Review</u>
</b><br/>When I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1099301.The_Name_of_This_Book_Is_Secret__Secret___1_' title='The Name of This Book Is Secret (Secret, #1) by Pseudonymous Bosch' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Name of This Book Is Secret</a> I thought it was fantastic! For some odd reason though, I did not get around to continuing the series until now, almost seven years after reading the first book. I think I tried to check this book out from the library, but it wasn't available so it was forgotten. This book does a great job of catching the reader up on previous events with little footnotes and summaries</span>
  <span id="freeText4861020228151253068" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a> <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Short and Simple Review</u>
</b><br />When I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1099301.The_Name_of_This_Book_Is_Secret__Secret___1_" title="The Name of This Book Is Secret (Secret, #1) by Pseudonymous Bosch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Name of This Book Is Secret</a> I thought it was fantastic! For some odd reason though, I did not get around to continuing the series until now, almost seven years after reading the first book. I think I tried to check this book out from the library, but it wasn't available so it was forgotten. This book does a great job of catching the reader up on previous events with little footnotes and summaries for those like me who couldn't remember the first book. I actually got into this book fairly quickly and I immensely enjoyed it. This is such an odd series and I love it for that! Some elements in the book feel so random, but everything is still so thought out! I really love how the book is narrated and how Bosch engages the reader, the book written as if talking to the reader, and all the measures Bosch goes through to keep the secret hidden! Overall, even though it has been a while, I was still able to enjoy this book and my feelings towards the series remain positive. I also made sure to check the next book out of the library immediately so the same mistake wouldn't happen again.</span>

<div id="review_2970704267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2970704267" />
    <a title="Caridee Chau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101537808-caridee-chau"><img alt="Caridee Chau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566707322p2/101537808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2970704267?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caridee Chau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caridee Chau" href="/user/show/101537808-caridee-chau">Caridee Chau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9787534650826" href="/book/show/41596598-if-youre-reading-this-its-too-late">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2970704267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9027320978533414211">This is the second in a series of five books in the secret series by Pseudonymous Bosch. This book is about the endeavour of a teenage child immensely skilled in the art of surviving any type of deadly circumstance, a Japanese boy with a collection of brightly coloured articles of clothing, and a talkative boy who is allergic to chocolate (or so he thinks). The three have one thing in common: they are members of the Terces society and their mission is do discover the long lost secret that has th</span>
  <span id="freeText9027320978533414211" style="display:none">This is the second in a series of five books in the secret series by Pseudonymous Bosch. This book is about the endeavour of a teenage child immensely skilled in the art of surviving any type of deadly circumstance, a Japanese boy with a collection of brightly coloured articles of clothing, and a talkative boy who is allergic to chocolate (or so he thinks). The three have one thing in common: they are members of the Terces society and their mission is do discover the long lost secret that has the potential to do unlimited damage to the world as our protagonists know it. However, this secret also has the potential to help the world in numerous ways. With a new lead, the three agents are tugged into a perilous adventure. <br /><br />I enjoyed this book because the writer effectively draws suspense and tension in his words. This made the book more interesting to the reader and made me wonder what was going to happen next. The writer also switches between different perspectives throughout the story, giving the reader a omniscient view of the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9027320978533414211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bedelya (clockwork.bookdragon) Moreno-Roth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bedelya (clockwork.bookdragon) Moreno-Roth" href="/user/show/75805693-bedelya-clockwork-bookdragon-moreno-roth">Bedelya (clockwork.bookdragon) Moreno-Roth</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277350816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6253033456583910773">If you are reading this, it’s too late....because I have finished this book! I liked this book but it’s very different from what I usually read. Part of the story seems to contain “magic” yet it still tries to be grounded in reality. There is a lot of plot convenient scenarios that doesn’t seem plausible. Then again that maybe the point of the entire series. It may also be that it is a middle grade book so it can get away with being a bit more fantastical, however I have read other middle grade </span>
  <span id="freeText6253033456583910773" style="display:none">If you are reading this, it’s too late....because I have finished this book! I liked this book but it’s very different from what I usually read. Part of the story seems to contain “magic” yet it still tries to be grounded in reality. There is a lot of plot convenient scenarios that doesn’t seem plausible. Then again that maybe the point of the entire series. It may also be that it is a middle grade book so it can get away with being a bit more fantastical, however I have read other middle grade books that have tackled these themes with better success. Don’t get me wrong the book is worth the read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6253033456583910773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dYKqBCq0kltWx/YrURhF+o/xgXayeg/40VQW+z9BWYlAyOYcf04Bwx/yJ/vfFmAeuUAUSZmUUivygZPpDIzuLA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ycxocp7QjWjalbFjU7oinvSpwge8yrBUqjByu3J25mn8hiRqyyoe8JOgYLPdtAd6whhXOJck7YeJ5fepQbtRzA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11994692556933258803">Pseudonymous Bosch is the infamously anonymous author of the New York Times bestselling Secret Series and the Bad Books. Despite rumors to the contrary, his books are not actually written by his pet rabbit, Quiche; the rabbit is merely his typist.</span>
